Fix any issues found.\n\n## Phase 1: Identify Changes\n\nRun `git diff` (or `git diff HEAD` if there are staged changes) to see what changed. If there are no git changes, review the most recently modified files that the user mentioned or that you edited earlier in this conversation.\n\n## Phase 2: Launch Three Review Agents in Parallel\n\nUse the Agent tool to launch all three agents concurrently in a single message. Pass each agent the full diff so it has the complete context.\n\n### Agent 1: Code Reuse Review\n\nFor each change:\n\n1. **Search for existing utilities and helpers** that could replace newly written code. Use Grep to find similar patterns elsewhere in the codebase — common locations are utility directories, shared modules, and files adjacent to the changed ones.\n2. **Flag any new function that duplicates existing functionality.** Suggest the existing function to use instead.\n3. **Flag any inline logic that could use an existing utility** — hand-rolled string manipulation, manual path handling, custom environment checks, ad-hoc type guards, and similar patterns are common candidates.\n\n### Agent 2: Code Quality Review\n\nReview the same changes for hacky patterns:\n\n1. **Redundant state**: state that duplicates existing state, cached values that could be derived, observers/effects that could be direct calls\n2. **Parameter sprawl**: adding new parameters to a function instead of generalizing or restructuring existing ones\n3. **Copy-paste with slight variation**: near-duplicate code blocks that should be unified with a shared abstraction\n4. **Leaky abstractions**: exposing internal details that should be encapsulated, or breaking existing abstraction boundaries\n5. **Stringly-typed code**: using raw strings where constants, enums (string unions), or branded types already exist in the codebase\n\n### Agent 3: Efficiency Review\n\nReview the same changes for efficiency:\n\n1. **Unnecessary work**: redundant computations, repeated file reads, duplicate network/API calls, N+1 patterns\n2. **Missed concurrency**: independent operations run sequentially when they could run in parallel\n3. **Hot-path bloat**: new blocking work added to startup or per-request/per-render hot paths\n4. **Unnecessary existence checks**: pre-checking file/resource existence before operating (TOCTOU anti-pattern) — operate directly and handle the error\n5. **Memory**: unbounded data structures, missing cleanup, event listener leaks\n6. **Overly broad operations**: reading entire files when only a portion is needed, loading all items when filtering for one\n\n## Phase 3: Fix Issues\n\nWait for all three agents to complete. Aggregate their findings and fix each issue directly. If a finding is a false positive or not worth addressing, note it and move on — do not argue with the finding, just skip it.\n\nWhen done, briefly summarize what was fixed (or confirm the code was already clean).\n\n\n## Additional Focus\n\ninternal/command/format/compact.go internal/command/format/compact_test.go"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"90978072-d55e-4370-b94c-ff1340a79cd8","uuid":"c97b02cd-984b-4e79-8130-1069d6f6d3f6","isSynthetic":true}

Although the long-form text parts of the message are wrapped,\n    32→// not all aspects of the message are guaranteed to fit within the specified\n    33→// terminal width.\n    34→func a nil diagnostic in here...\n    41→\t\treturn \"\"\n    42→\t}\n    43→\n    44→\tvar buf bytes.Buffer\n    45→\n    46→\t// these leftRule* variables are markers for the beginning of the lines\n    47→\t// containing the diagnostic that are intended to help sighted users\n    48→\t// better understand the information hierarchy when diagnostics appear\n    49→\t// alongside other information or alongside other diagnostics.\n    50→\t//\n    51→\t// Without this, it seems (based on folks sharing incomplete messages when\n    52→\t// asking questions, or including extra content that's not part of the\n    53→\t// diagnostic) that some readers have trouble easily identifying which\n    54→\t// text belongs to the diagnostic and which does not.\n    55→\tvar leftRuleLine, leftRuleStart, leftRuleEnd string\n    56→\tvar leftRuleWidth int // in visual character cells\n    57→\n    58→\tswitch diag.Severity {\n    59→\tcase viewsjson.DiagnosticSeverityError:\n    60→\t\tbuf.WriteString(color.Color(\"[bold][red]Error: [reset]\"))\n    61→\t\tleftRuleLine = color.Color(\"[red]│[reset] \")\n    62→\t\tleftRuleStart = color.Color(\"[red]╷[reset]\")\n    63→\t\tleftRuleEnd = color.Color(\"[red]╵[reset]\")\n    64→\t\tleftRuleWidth = 2\n    65→\tcase viewsjson.DiagnosticSeverityWarning:\n    66→\t\tbuf.WriteString(color.Color(\"[bold][yellow]Warning: [reset]\"))\n    67→\t\tleftRuleLine = color.Color(\"[yellow]│[reset] \")\n    68→\t\tleftRuleStart = color.Color(\"[yellow]╷[reset]\")\n    69→\t\tleftRuleEnd = color.Color(\"[yellow]╵[reset]\")\n    70→\t\tleftRuleWidth = 2\n    71→\tdefault:\n    72→\t\t// Clear out any coloring that might be applied by Terraform's UI helper,\n    73→\t\t// so our result is not context-sensitive.\n    74→\t\tbuf.WriteString(color.Color(\"\\n[reset]\"))\n    75→\t}\n    76→\n    77→\t// We don't wrap the summary, since we expect it to be terse, and since\n    78→\t// this is where we put the text of a native Go error it may not always\n    79→\t// be pure text that lends itself well to word-wrapping.\n    80→\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, color.Color(\"[bold]%s[reset]\\n\\n\"), diag.Summary)\n    81→\n    82→\tf := &snippetFormatter{&buf, diag, color}\n    83→\tf.write()\n    84→\n    85→\tif diag.Detail != \"\" {\n    86→\t\tparaWidth := width - leftRuleWidth - 1 // leave room for the left rule\n    87→\t\tif paraWidth > 0 {\n    88→\t\t\tlines := strings.Split(diag.Detail, \"\\n\")\n    89→\t\t\tfor _, line := range lines {\n    90→\t\t\t\tif !strings.HasPrefix(line, \" \") {\n    91→\t\t\t\t\tline = wordwrap.WrapString(color.Color(line), uint(paraWidth))\n    92→\t\t\t\t}\n    93→\t\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"%s\\n\", line)\n    94→\t\t\t}\n    95→\t\t} else {\n    96→\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"%s\\n\", diag.Detail)\n    97→\t\t}\n    98→\t}\n    99→\n   100→\t// Before we return, we'll finally add the left rule prefixes to each\n   101→\t// line so that the overall message is visually delimited from what's\n   102→\t// around it. We'll do that by scanning over what we already generated\n   103→\t// and adding the prefix for each line.\n   104→\tvar ruleBuf strings.Builder\n   105→\tsc := bufio.NewScanner(&buf)\n   106→\truleBuf.WriteString(leftRuleStart)\n   107→\truleBuf.WriteByte('\\n')\n   108→\tfor sc.Scan() {\n   109→\t\tline := sc.Text()\n   110→\t\tprefix := leftRuleLine\n   111→\t\tif line == \"\" {\n   112→\t\t\t// Don't print the space after the line if there would be nothing\n   113→\t\t\t// after it anyway.\n   114→\t\t\tprefix = strings.TrimSpace(prefix)\n   115→\t\t}\n   116→\t\truleBuf.WriteString(prefix)\n   117→\t\truleBuf.WriteString(line)\n   118→\t\truleBuf.WriteByte('\\n')\n   119→\t}\n   120→\truleBuf.WriteString(leftRuleEnd)\n   121→\truleBuf.WriteByte('\\n')\n   122→\n   123→\treturn ruleBuf.String()\n   124→}\n   125→\n   126→// DiagnosticPlain is an alternative to Diagnostic which minimises the use of\n   127→// virtual terminal formatting sequences.\n   128→//\n   129→// It is intended for use in automation and other contexts in which diagnostic\n   130→// messages are parsed from the Terraform output.\n   131→func 135→func DiagnosticPlainFromJSON(diag *viewsjson.Diagnostic, width int) string {\n   136→\tif diag == nil {\n   137→\t\t// No good reason to pass a nil diagnostic in here...\n   138→\t\treturn \"\"\n   139→\t}\n   140→\n   141→\tvar buf bytes.Buffer\n   142→\n   143→\tswitch diag.Severity {\n   144→\tcase viewsjson.DiagnosticSeverityError:\n   145→\t\tbuf.WriteString(\"\\nError: \")\n   146→\tcase 161→\t\tif width > 1 {\n   162→\t\t\tlines := strings.Split(diag.Detail, \"\\n\")\n   163→\t\t\tfor _, line := range lines {\n   164→\t\t\t\tif !strings.HasPrefix(line, \" \") {\n   165→\t\t\t\t\tline 218→\n   219→\treturn b.String()\n   220→}\n   221→\n   222→// snippetFormatter handles formatting diagnostic information with source snippets\n   223→type snippetFormatter struct {\n   224→\tbuf *snippetFormatter) writeSnippet(snippet *viewsjson.DiagnosticSnippet, code string) {\n   266→\tbuf := f.buf\n   267→\tcolor := f.color\n   268→\n   269→\t// Split the snippet and render the 284→\t// this would happen only if there's a bug in the code generating\n   285→\t// the snippet objects.\n   286→\tif start < 0 {\n   287→\t\tstart = 0\n   288→\t} else if start > len(code) {\n   289→\t\tstart = len(code)\n   290→\t}\n   291→\tif end < 0 {\n   292→\t\tend = 0\n   293→\t} else if end > len(code) {\n   294→\t\tend = len(code)\n   295→\t}\n   296→\n   297→\tbefore, highlight, snippet.TestAssertionExpr != nil {\n   311→\t\t// The diagnostic may also have information about the dynamic\n   312→\t\t// values of relevant variables at the point of evaluation.\n   313→\t\t// This  375→\t// for the test assertion.\n   376→\tif diag.ShowVerbose {\n   377→\t\tfmt.Fprint(buf, color.Color(\"    [dark_gray]│[reset] [bold]LHS[reset]:\\n\"))\n   378→\t\tfor line := range 411→\tprintLine := func(prefix, line string) {\n   412→\t\tvar colour string\n   413→\t\tswitch prefix {\n   414→\t\tcase \"-\":\n   415→\t\t\tcolour = \"[red]\"\n   416→\t\tcase \"+\":\n := make(map[plans.Action]string)\nactionStrings[plans.Create] = \"create\"\nactionStrings[plans.Update] = \"update\"\n// ... etc\n```\n\n**Problem**: \n- The `plans.Action` type already has a generated `String()` method (in `/workspace/internal/plans/action_string.go`) via `go:generate stringer`\n- These hardcoded strings duplicate the canonical source of action names\n- The mapping is incorrect: `actionStrings[plans.Create]` returns `\"create\"` but `plans.Create.String()` returns `\"Create\"`\n- Inconsistent with the `actionDescription()` function in `/workspace/internal/command/jsonformat/plan.go` which uses the String() method\n\n**Recommendation**: Create a function that converts Action.String() output to the desired format:\n```go\nfunc humanReadableAction(action plans.Action) string {\n    s := action.String()\n    if s == \"\" {\n        return \"\"\n    }\n    // Convert \"Create\" -> \"create\", \"DeleteThenCreate\" -> \"replace\", etc.\n    // ... conversion logic\n}\n```\n\nOr better yet, add a method to `plans.Action` in the plans package.\n\n---\n\n### 2. **Copy-Paste Code - Repetitive Summary Building** (HIGH)\n\n**Issue**: Lines 105-138 contain highly repetitive code that builds summary items:\n```go\ncreateCount := counts[plans.Create]\nif createCount > 0 {\n    summaryItems = append(summaryItems, fmt.Sprintf(\"Plan: %d to add\", createCount))\n}\n\nupdateCount := counts[plans.Update]\nif updateCount > 0 {\n    summaryItems = append(summaryItems, fmt.Sprintf(\"%d to change\", updateCount))\n}\n\nreplaceCount := counts[plans.DeleteThenCreate] + counts[plans.CreateThenDelete]\nif replaceCount > 0 {\n    summaryItems = append(summaryItems, fmt.Sprintf(\"%d to replace\", replaceCount))\n}\n// ... repeated pattern 5 more times\n```\n\n**Problem**:\n- Each action type follows an identical pattern (extract count, check > 0, format string)\n- Only the action constant, label string, and format vary\n- This is error-prone for maintenance and adding new action types\n- Violates DRY principle\n\n**Recommendation**: Create a helper structure to drive the summary building:\n```go\ntype summaryItem struct {\n    actions []plans.Action\n    label   string\n    format  string\n}\n\nsummarySpecs := []summaryItem{\n    {[]plans.Action{plans.Create}, \"Plan: %d to add\", \"add\"},\n    {[]plans.Action{plans.Update}, \"%d to change\", \"change\"},\n    // ... etc\n}\n\nfor _, spec := range summarySpecs {\n    count := 0\n    for _, action := range spec.actions {\n        count += counts[action]\n    }\n    if count > 0 {\n        summaryItems = append(summaryItems, fmt.Sprintf(spec.format, count))\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### 3. **String Concatenation Loop** (MEDIUM)\n\n**Issue**: Lines 141-148 build the summary string with inefficient concatenation:\n```go\nsummary := \"\"\nfor i, item := range summaryItems {\n    if i == 0 {\n        summary = item\n    } else {\n        summary += \", \" + item  // String concatenation in loop\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Problem**:\n- Uses string concatenation in a loop (inefficient, creates new strings each iteration)\n- Go provides `strings.Join()` for this exact purpose\n\n**Recommendation**:\n```go\nsummary := strings.Join(summaryItems, \", \")\n```\n\n---\n\n### 4. **Inconsistent Action Order Definition** (MEDIUM)\n\n**Issue**: Lines 44-53 define `actionOrder` hardcoded slice, but this duplicate information should be centralized.\n\n**Problem**:\n- The order is duplicated from the `actionStrings` map iteration order\n- If a new action type is added to `plans.Action`, developers must remember to update both places\n- No validation that all actions in `actionStrings` are in `actionOrder`\n- The mapping between action order (for display) and action strings (for labels) is implicit and fragile\n\n**Recommendation**: Generate this order from a centralized mapping or use a constant in the plans package.\n\n---\n\n### 5. **Redundant hasChanges Check** (LOW)\n\n**Issue**: Lines 92-98:\n```go\nhasChanges := false\nfor _, count := range counts {\n    if count > 0 {\n        hasChanges = true\n        break\n    }\n}\n\nif hasChanges {\n    // ... build summary\n}\n```\n\n**Problem**:\n- This can be simplified: check if `len(summaryItems) > 0` after building them\n- Or use a simpler pattern\n\n**Recommendation**:\n```go\nif len(summaryItems) > 0 {\n    // ... build summary\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### 6. **Redundant Nil Checks in Loop** (LOW)\n\n**Issue**: Lines 83-85:\n```go\nfor _, resource := range resources {\n    if resource == nil {\n        continue\n    }\n```\n\n**Problem**:\n- The resource slice is populated from `plan.Changes.Resources` with a filter (lines 33-40)\n- Only non-nil resources are appended to the `changes` map\n- Therefore, `resource` should never be nil here\n- This check is redundant defensive programming\n\n**Recommendation**: Remove the nil check or add a comment explaining why it's necessary for safety.\n\n---\n\n### 7. **Inconsistency with JSON Formatter** (MEDIUM)\n\n**Issue**: The
